Local News

Inauguration Ceremony of the January 28th Memorial Hall Held Yesterday by the Garrison Headquarters 118

More than 600 Representatives from All Circles Attended

Mayor Wu and Others Delivered Moving Speeches

The Atmosphere Was Exceptionally Solemn and Enthusiastic

The January 28th Memorial Hall of the Longhua Songhu Garrison Headquarters held its inauguration ceremony at 10:00 AM yesterday. A total of more than 600 guests from various agencies and organizations attended. Garrison Commander Dai Ji presided over the ceremony and reported on the significance and process of building the January 28th Memorial Hall. Mayor Wu and others delivered heartfelt speeches. The arrangement inside the hall was cautionary, and the atmosphere of the meeting place was solemn. The ceremony concluded at around 12:00 PM. Details are described below.

A Glimpse Outside the Venue 119

Starting at 8:00 AM yesterday, the Security Department deployed guards on Longhua Road. Inside the Garrison Headquarters, the Garrison troops were on special alert. Above the main gate, on both the east and west sides, hung horizontal banners that read "Inauguration Ceremony of the January 28th Memorial Hall." A large, colorful archway commemorating "January 28th" was erected at the entrance, with large crossed Party and national flags on both sides. Various cautionary slogans were posted along Longhua Road and inside the Garrison Headquarters. Four reception rooms were set up in the Garrison Headquarters office, where staff members of the headquarters served refreshments to the guests in a very thoughtful manner.

Arrangement of the Auditorium 120

The January 28th Memorial Hall was arranged very exquisitely. In the center hung the Party and national flags and the portrait and last will of Sun Yat-sen. Small Party and national flags were hung on all four sides of the hall. On both sides of the front were hung portraits of Chairman Lin of the National Government, President Wang, Chairman Jiang, and Minister He. On the four walls were hung portraits of anti-Japanese generals Chen Mingshu, Jiang Guangnai, Cai Tingkai, Dai Ji, Zhang Zhizhong, and senior officers of the 19th Route Army and the 5th Army, as well as portraits of fallen soldiers. Seven large and small oil paintings depicting anti-Japanese warfare were hung on the pillars on both sides of the hall, which were startling. There were also various statistical charts on participating in the anti-Japanese resistance, as well as framed couplets sent by various circles, which were also hung on the walls. What was most noteworthy was that the seating arrangement for the guests was in the shape of "128". Famous oil paintings, such as the 19th Route Army holding a military conference and the Japanese army attacking Wusong by sea and air, were displayed. Among them, one of the most startling paintings was the street battle in front of the Commercial Press on Baoshan Road in Zhabei. At a glance, one could immediately recall the old scenes of the January 28th battle last year, lingering in one's mind and unable to be erased.

Participating Guests 121

In addition to Songhu Garrison Commander Dai Ji, Chief of Staff Zhang Xiang, and all officers, those who attended the ceremony included Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Wu Guangxin representing Central Bank Governor Kong Xiangxi, Municipal Government Secretary-General Yu Hongjun, Municipal Councilors Yu Qiaqing and Du Yuesheng, Security Department Director Yang Hu, Public Security Bureau Director Wen Hongen, Public Works Bureau Director Xu Peihuang, Works Bureau Director Shen Yi, Health Bureau Director Li Ting'an, Public Security Bureau Inspector Gong Xikui, Municipal Party Committee Member Jiang Huaishu, Supervisory Yuan Member Gao Yihan, Relief Committee Chairman Xu Shiying, 19th Route Army Representative Huang Hechun, 88th Division Representative Ye Fei, Commander of the First Fleet of the Navy Chen Jiliang, Jianghai Customs Superintendent Tang Hai'an, Head of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Zhao Tiezhang, Director of the Two Roads Administration Huang Boqiao, Municipal Chamber of Commerce Luo Qinghua, Secretary-General of the Bankers' Association Lin Kanghou, Zhang Tianfu of the First Special District Local Court, Ying Shi of the Second Special District Local Court, Liang Renjie of the Second Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court, He Yitu of the Shanghai County Government, Yao Wenjun of the Baoshan County Government, Rong Yufeng of the Telegraph Bureau, Xu Xueyu of the Telephone Bureau, Chu Fucheng and Zhu Qinglan of the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army Support Association, as well as representatives from various circles and reporters from various newspapers, approximately 600 people.

Details of the Ceremony 122

Garrison Commander Dai Ji served as the chairman and appointed Adjutant Zhang Yusan as the master of ceremonies. After the meeting began, the ceremony was conducted in the prescribed order. (1) When the Garrison Band played military music, everyone stood up and paid their respects in unison. (2) Amidst the sound of firecrackers, the national flag was raised with the sounding of bugles. (3) The Party song was sung. (4) The highest salute was paid to the Party and national flags and the portrait of Sun Yat-sen. (5) Chairman Dai Ji respectfully read Sun Yat-sen's last will. (6) The highest salute was paid to the citizens, soldiers, and police who died in the January 28th Incident. (7) Three minutes of silence were observed. The atmosphere at the venue was silent at the time, and extremely solemn.

Chairman's Report 123

After the ceremony was conducted as prescribed, Garrison Commander Dai Ji, as chairman, reported: "Ladies and gentlemen, representatives from all circles, today is the day of the inauguration of the January 28th Memorial Hall of our headquarters. We are truly honored that you have come from afar to participate, despite the summer heat. However, preparations were too rushed, and there are too many imperfections. We hope you will point them out. The hospitality is also inadequate, and we hope you will forgive us. I will now report to you on the process of preparing this hall. The January 28th Incident is a day worth commemorating, and I believe that most of you share this sentiment, especially the people of Shanghai, who suffered deeply and should never forget it. After the January 28th battle, I wanted to create something to mark this everlasting commemoration, to prevent the people of Shanghai from forgetting this trauma, and to stimulate the people of Shanghai not to let their enthusiasm for revenge and wiping out the humiliation cool down. However, due to limited funds, the matter did not come to fruition. Later, when I saw Zhabei preparing to build a Tomb of Unknown Heroes, I felt even more that the Nanshi area should also have a building with the same purpose. It just so happened that the auditorium of our headquarters had been in disrepair for many years and was about to collapse. After the central government sent people to investigate, they allocated several thousand yuan for reconstruction. I took this opportunity to take advantage of this small amount of money to transform the auditorium and name it the January 28th Memorial Hall to serve as a permanent memorial to the January 28th Shanghai battle. Although it was built with limited resources, it was significant that the memorial hall was located in Longhua, where I had made decisions with Mr. Jiang and Mr. Cai before the war. So I opened up a barren land to the west of the hall, built a pavilion and planted trees, and erected a monument on the small hill as a record. The pavilion and garden are both named after January 28th to mark the everlasting commemoration. The entire project took less than two months from start to finish, and due to limited funds, I could only proceed with limited resources. Initially, the plan was to create eleven large and small murals in the hall and collect various January 28th publications, photographs, and war trophies for observation. However, due to funding issues, I reluctantly created one large painting and six small paintings. Also, because I was transferred to Fujian, I had to quickly complete it in a short period of time. The collection of items is not yet complete, and even the items from the 19th Route Army have not been sent. It is still far from what was initially planned. At this time, it is only a rough outline. How to enrich it and how to adorn it in the future depends on the assistance of my colleagues and gentlemen from all walks of life. Most of the items collected in this hall were donated by various agencies, bookstores, newspapers, and film companies. We have only slightly organized them, divided them into charts, and pasted them into albums for display. I should thank all the donors. The News, the Shih Pao, and the Times each donated the entire newspaper from the time of the burning of the Sanyou Society to the withdrawal of troops during the Shanghai battle. These are very rare and valuable souvenirs, and I am extremely grateful. Also, Mr. Zhang Yunqiao, who painted the murals for us, worked tirelessly and volunteered his services. He completed all the paintings in two weeks, and his spirit is admirable. This is something we are especially grateful for. Today, I would also like to express my gratitude for the many precious items that people from all walks of life have sent to enrich this hall. I will never forget these things. Today, I would like to express my gratitude for all of these things here. Finally, I have a few words to say. I have been in Shanghai for a long time, and twenty months have passed in a flash. In these twenty months, I have not done anything, but all of you gentlemen and people from all walks of life have always been helping me. I am very grateful for this kindness, and I also feel very ashamed. Fortunately, there have not been any major incidents in these twenty months, which has allowed me to fulfill my passive responsibilities. This is all thanks to the guidance and assistance, both tangible and intangible, of all of you gentlemen and people from all walks of life. I rarely have the opportunity to gather with you. Although it is not yet certain whether I will go to Fujian, I will be leaving Shanghai soon. Today, I would like to take this opportunity to say goodbye to you, and at the same time, I have a request to make of you. Even though I am leaving this place and leaving you, I still hope that you will give me your guidance and assistance at any time, just as if I were still by your side. I feel that what can be separated in life is the form, but the spirit will never be separated. What do you think? I think you will all agree to my request and help me achieve this hope."

Mayor's Speech 124

After the Chairman's report, Mayor Wu Tiecheng gave a speech, saying, "The late Premier Sun Yat-sen said that it is not necessary for a person to become a high official, but it is necessary to do great things." I believe that to do great things, one must first establish a goal and make a firm resolution in order to succeed in a lasting and immortal undertaking. Considering the four days before the January 28th Incident, which was January 24th, Commander Dai and General Commander Chiang Kai-shek, along with Military Commander Cai, held a meeting and made a firm decision to defend Shanghai to the death. This led to the January 28th Resistance against Japan, which added a page of self-respect and glory to the history of the Chinese nation. Today, the significance of Commander Dai's construction of the January 28th Memorial Hall is threefold: first, to commemorate the advance resolution of the January 28th Resistance against Japan warriors; second, to teach about shame and war, inspiring the citizens' awareness; and third, for our compatriots across the country to never forget the officers and soldiers who sacrificed themselves here when they see this January 28th Memorial Hall. Shanghai, as a corner, is the gateway to the capital, the barrier of the central hub for issuing orders, and the center of the national economy and the starting point for national undertakings. The safety of Shanghai is related to the national lifeline. With the meager forces of the 19th Route Army and the 5th Army, and with inferior equipment, we resisted the power of the Japanese navy, army, and air force, maintaining safety. The resolution of a few people has accomplished this great undertaking, which can truly be called a lasting and immortal achievement. We should never forget it. Today, as we come to attend the completion ceremony of the January 28th Memorial Hall, I would like to contribute and encourage myself to all compatriots across the country. All Shanghai citizens should especially not forget Commander Dai's great achievements. Now that Commander Dai is about to leave us, the citizens of Shanghai should express their gratitude to this key figure who stabilized Shanghai during the extremely difficult January 28th Resistance against Japan for more than twenty months."

Other Speeches 125

In addition to Mayor Wu, guest speakers also included Jiang Huaixu, representing the Municipal Party Committee; Ye Fei, representing the 88th Division; Huang Hechun, director of the 19th Route Army's Beijing Office; Yang Hu, head of the Security Department; and Zhu Qinglan, Lin Kanghou, and Sun Weifan. Jiang Huaixu expressed his hope that the day the January 28th Memorial Hall is demolished will be the day our country avenges its shame. Ye Fei expressed his hope that all compatriots across the country will mobilize and overthrow imperialism. Huang Hechun expressed his hope that the people of the country will continue to work hard, carrying forward the spirit of the soldiers and civilians who died in the January 28th Incident. Zhu Qinglan stated that the January 28th Memorial Hall is a memorial to: (1) the great spirit of the Chinese nation, (2) the determination of the soldiers to defend the country, and (3) the power of cooperation between the military and the people. Lin Kanghou briefly stated that those in power must like what the people like and hate what the people hate, so that cooperation can be effective and we can unite against foreign enemies. The January 28th Incident is an example of this, and so on.

Unveiling Ceremony 126

Behind the memorial hall is the memorial garden, which contains earthen mounds and cement steps, where flowers and trees can be planted in stages. At the top of the mound is the memorial碑to the officers and soldiers who died in the January 28th Incident, covered with the party-state flag. After the completion ceremony, Commander Dai unveiled the party-state flag amidst the sound of music, and then paid his respects to the 碑. After the ceremony, the meeting was adjourned.

A Glimpse of Slogans 127

Various slogans were posted inside and outside the venue and along Longhua Road, as follows: (1) Commemorating January 28th is preparation for revenge and washing away shame. (1) Advance on the blood of the martyrs of the January 28th Incident. (1) January 28th is the spirit of awakening the people to resist insults and save the country. (1) January 28th is a manifestation of the power of the Shanghai people. (1) Commemorating January 28th means promoting the spirit of saving the country and eliminating traitors. (1) Commemorating January 28th means uniting to resist foreign aggression. (1) Commemorating January 28th means carrying out the Premier's last will and reforming internal affairs. (1) Commemorating January 28th means not forgetting May 7th and September 18th. (1) Avenge the civilians, soldiers, and police who died in the January 28th Incident, etc.

Various Statistics 128

The various statistical charts displayed in the memorial hall were very eye-catching. They are recorded as follows: (1) Statistical chart of the losses suffered by all sectors of Shanghai during the January 28th Bloody Battle (in yuan): Temples and monasteries 154,720.00; Parks 1,445,440.32; Schools 3,094,630.50; Railways 16,893,317.64; Institutions 22,628,717.85; Shops 49,496,508.32; Households 50,989,296.10; Factories 59,814,720.32; Total 211,499,680.45; (2) Statistical chart of the bullets received by the officers and soldiers wounded in the January 28th Battle (in percentage): Those killed by dumdum bullets 63%; Those killed by ordinary bullets 9%; Those killed by bombs 12%; Those killed by shells 17%; (3) Comparative table of soldiers killed in action by various armies in the January 28th Songhu Resistance against Japan (in people): 78th Division 1128; 88th Division 1019; 61st Division 846; 87th Division 499; 60th Division 394; Tax Police Regiment 210; Military Police Regiment 26; (4) Comparative table of officers killed in action in our army in the January 28th Incident (in people): 88th Division 58; 61st Division 46; 78th Division 45; 60th Division 28; 87th Division 24; Tax Police Regiment 15; (5) Comparative table of officers wounded in action in the January 28th Songhu Resistance against Japan (in people): Military Police Regiment 2; Police 4; Tax Police Regiment 33; 60th Division 928; 87th Division 101; 88th Division 142; 61st Division 195.

Open to the Public 129

After the completion ceremony of the January 28th Memorial Hall yesterday, in order to allow people from all walks of life to understand the truth of the Songhu Battle, it was specifically decided to open it for two days, August 11th and 12th, for people to visit. Members of the Garrison Command were dispatched to receive visitors. In the future, it will be open to the public on all National Humiliation Memorial Days to show commemoration.

Zhu Qinglan Cables Li Du 130

Requesting investigation of claims regarding the four-six split, etc.

Zhu claims all donations have receipts as proof

The public should be openly informed of any doubts

Regarding the issue of donations for resisting Japan and saving the nation, since Ma Zhanshan announced the detailed amount of donations he received, various organizations have been conducting investigations. On August 2nd, General Zhu Qinglan received a cable from General Li Du inquiring about the anti-Japanese donations. He immediately replied with an airmail cable, explaining the process of the donations. However, on the 8th, the "Jing Bao" newspaper in this city published a news article of an interview with General Li Du, which raised doubts about General Zhu. Zhu sent another cable to General Li Du on the 9th, requesting an investigation. The details are as follows:

Zhu Qinglan's Remarks 131

Yesterday morning, a reporter from this newspaper interviewed General Zhu Qinglan, asking about the points raised in General Li Du's cable. According to him, he did indeed receive Li's cable on the 2nd of this month and immediately replied by express airmail cable. However, upon recently reading the "Jing Bao" containing a record of an interview with General Li, there were claims of a four-six split of the donations and the establishment of a school with 500,000 yuan. These claims are completely untrue and he does not know what they are based on. He cabled Li yesterday to request an investigation, because personal reputation is a small matter, but the future of resisting Japan is of great importance. All the donations he handled were used according to the purposes designated by the donors, and the donors were informed separately. Reports were also made for donations without designated purposes. Those remitted through banks also have official receipts from the banks. The accounts of donations and payments received by the local Righteous Army Support Association, the Northeast Refugee Relief Association, and other organizations are reported every ten days and sent to the donors. The procedures are extremely clear. The public should be openly informed of any questions, and all have receipts as proof, etc.

General Li's Cable to Zhu 132

General Li Du's cable to General Zhu Qinglan reads: Since the September 18th Incident, compatriots at home and abroad have enthusiastically supported the Northeast Anti-Japanese Armies, donating generously. In reality, the various units of the Northeast Anti-Japanese forces received very few of these donations. During the intense fighting, patriotic heroes shed blood on the battlefield, and the elders and children were trampled under the iron hooves of the enemy. It was tragic and heartbreaking, until we were exhausted and the Northeast fell. It is said that Mr. Zhu has received more than 3.8 million yuan in donations. Who exactly did you assist? There are many misunderstandings among the various parties, saying that Mr. Zhu has been deceived. I hope you will publish in the newspapers the detailed amount and purpose of each donation you have received, to comfort the people of the country. This not only concerns personal integrity, but also concerns the kind people who have ruined their families to relieve the country's difficulties and the gentlemen who have generously rewarded the troops. If they know that the use is improper, they will lose faith. Who will still be willing to do what is right? This is of utmost importance to the future of the national crisis. I remember that you, sir, have long been admired by the people for rescuing the afflicted and helping the needy. This is precisely to maintain your good name, not because I personally have any dissatisfaction. I hope you understand. Li Du bows.

Zhu Cables Request for Investigation 133

General Zhu Qinglan sent another cable to General Li Du on the 9th, requesting an investigation. The original cable reads: Mr. Li Zhichu, Gu Ling Xun Jian: I received your cable and replied with a winter cable sent by airmail, which should have reached you long ago. Recently, I saw a news article in the Shanghai "Jing Bao" on August 8th, a record of an interview with General Li Du. The original article recorded your conversation with the interviewee regarding anti-Japanese donations, including the following paragraph: "We issue a receipt for 10,000 yuan, but actually only receive 6,000 yuan. The remaining 40% is taken by General Zhu to be used for anti-Japanese purposes, a four-six split. We alone take the credit for it. Also, General Zhu used 500,000 yuan of the donations to establish a school. Although running a school is also beneficial to the country, it seems to deviate from the original intention of the public's donations." The above is all without any factual basis. Reading it makes me feel particularly lost. In addition to sending you the original newspaper, I have specifically listed the following points to clarify the truth: (1) Is the conversation recorded in the newspaper actually true? (2) If the conversation is true, then there are the following two points: "Issuing a receipt for 10,000 yuan, but actually only receiving 6,000 yuan," please point out the facts and the person in charge. (3) What is the basis for the so-called "using 500,000 yuan of the donations to establish a school"? Also, in your conversation, you said, "I heard that the amount donated in Shanghai does not match the amount received." I do not know who you heard it from. What is the fact that they do not match? This matter concerns public trust and affects the future of resisting Japan. I cannot remain silent. I hope you will clarify it to correct the hearing. Sincerely, Zhu Qinglan bows. Qing.

Preparing to Name Five Aircraft 139

Preparatory Committee of Five Organizations Holds Third Meeting Yesterday

Lin Wojang to Report on Reasons for Delayed Assembly

Li Dachao to Report on Reasons for Changing Venue

Resolution to Form Groups and Report on Donation Receipts

The joint naming ceremony for five aircraft has been postponed due to the assembly in Hangzhou not being completed in time. The preparatory committee of the five organizations held its third meeting yesterday. The details are as follows:

(Reasons for Delayed Assembly) Attendees: Li Dachao (Chairman), Lin Wojang, Mao Heyuan, Zhou Nianhang (Secretary), Wang Enchi, Wang Xianggao, Wang Gang. First, Lin Wojang reported on his visit to Hangzhou to inspect the assembly of the five aircraft. He briefly stated that after the preparatory committee decided to hold the five aircraft naming ceremony on August 12th, he immediately telegraphed the Hangzhou Aviation Department and sent a letter to the American mechanic responsible for assembling the five aircraft to urge him. Because he did not receive a definite reply, he went to Hangzhou on the evening of the 6th to inspect. Because only one American mechanic, Mr. Guler, and two assistants were responsible for assembling the five aircraft, and the workers of the Aviation Department were not able to participate, only three aircraft have been assembled. Testing the engines and measuring all the machinery will also take a considerable amount of time. It is estimated that they will be assembled around the 20th of this month. He has already asked the Aviation Department to inform them by telegram when the time comes, etc.

(Reasons for Changing Venue) Next, Li Dachao reported that the naming ceremony was originally planned to be held at the Jiangwan Racecourse. After he and Secretary Zhang Tingrong of the Municipal Government contacted the Shanghai Amateur Sports Federation, they agreed to lend it to them. However, because the location was too small to accommodate the take-off and landing of five aircraft, he and the Aviation Association discussed and decided to change the venue to the Hongqiao Airfield to avoid any danger. For the comfort and safety of the attendees, appropriate arrangements and convenient transportation should be arranged in advance, etc.

The date will be decided after receiving a telegram from the Aviation Department and convening another meeting. It was also decided to establish seven groups: Transportation, General Affairs, Reception, Arrangement, Security, Guard, and Publicity, to be responsible for handling the matters. The Municipal Government should increase the frequency of public buses to and from the arrangement and transportation aspects. The Municipal Government should rush to arrange it recently. The preparatory committee must go to inspect after the arrangement is appropriate. As for the fourth preparatory meeting, it should be convened temporarily when the time is right.

(Report on Donation Receipts) Then, Mao Heyuan reported that the Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association's aviation national salvation donations will be handed over to the Aviation Association in the next few days. If all the donations are more than enough to supply an aircraft, the surplus can be donated to the Ningbo No. 2 aircraft, etc. Wang Gang reported that the Boy Scouts Council handed over more than 20,000 yuan yesterday. Ye Xianggao reported that the General Labor Union had handed over 28,900 yuan yesterday. Finally, Zhou Nianhang reported that the General Team Leader's Office had received donations recently, including 16,085.20 yuan from the Shanghai Educational Association, 28,000 yuan from the Shanghai General Labor Union's Shanghai Workers' Aircraft Fundraising Committee, 3,000 yuan from the Shanghai Student Union of Secondary Schools, 9,500 yuan raised by Gu Jiatang, 4 silver dollars donated by Wang Desen, and 2 silver dollars donated by Gu Zhenyi, etc. The meeting then adjourned.

Negotiations for the Replacement of the Damaged Tianchu Aircraft 140

Decision in One Week

According to the National News Agency, the all-metal Tianchu fighter aircraft ordered by Tianchu Monosodium Glutamate Factory from the German Junkers Factory was damaged in a crash during a test flight. Because the aircraft has not been formally delivered, Tianchu Factory believes that the seller should be fully responsible. The Zenchhen Trading Company, which is managing the matter, believes that the test flight was insured at the time, so the insurance company cannot shirk its responsibility. The buyer, Tianchu Factory, has no responsibility whatsoever. The seller, Junkers Factory, the Zenchhen Trading Company, and the insurance company are currently studying the issue of responsibility. The procedures and methods for returning or replacing the aircraft can probably be decided within a week. However, Tianchu Monosodium Glutamate Factory believes that the deposit has been paid long ago, but the delivery has been delayed for various reasons. The interest on this large deposit should be moderately refunded by the seller to ensure fairness and avoid excessive losses. There has been no response to this point yet.

Opinions of Chinese-owned Cotton Mills on American Cotton Loans 142

According to the National News Agency, sources from Chinese-owned cotton mills revealed yesterday that domestic cotton supply has consistently fallen short of demand, making the purchase of American cotton for replenishment a common practice. For instance, last year, China produced 8 million dan of cotton (according to the China Cotton Industry Statistics Association's survey), while the cotton mills' demand reached 9 million dan (according to the Chinese Cotton Mill Owners' Association's survey). Additionally, about 4 million dan are estimated for cotton clothing linings. The deficit is naturally covered by imported cotton.

In the past twenty years, 4.8 million dan of cotton were imported, and 3.8 million dan in the twenty-first year. This year, due to the balancing of supply and demand, the shortfall is about 5 million dan. Moreover, Chinese-owned cotton mills are experiencing tight cash flow due to the aftermath of the January 28th Incident (Shanghai Incident of 1932). The exchange rate is unfavorable,

gold prices are too high, and domestic cotton prices are high while yarn prices are low, a difference of about 20 yuan. In desperation, many cotton mills have temporarily suspended operations. Minister Song Ziwen, taking the opportunity of attending the World Economic Conference and complying with the requests of domestic cotton mills, negotiated with the U.S. government for cotton and wheat loans. However, despite the U.S. government's successful efforts in maintaining ample supply of American cotton, prices have not fallen. It remains to be seen whether distressed Chinese-owned cotton mills can resume operations due to government purchases of large quantities of American cotton, as it depends on the cost. As for the government purchasing American cotton and then selling it to Japanese merchants, Chinese-owned cotton mills can only

express regret. The Chinese and Japanese cotton mills are fundamentally in a mutually exclusive position. If Japanese merchants need American cotton, they can directly order from American firms like Anderson, Clayton & Co. and Amcot, and the prices would be cheaper. The resale is actually done out of jealousy to prevent Chinese merchants from buying cotton and alleviate the cotton shortage, thereby weakening market competitors. Therefore, the purchase by Japanese merchants is not out of need, but

a competitive tactic. Chinese-owned cotton mills dare not oppose the government, nor can they oppose Japanese merchants. However, the government funding the market rivals of Chinese cotton mills is unwise and may be ridiculed. Chinese-owned cotton mills still hope that the rumors are untrue, or that Minister Song Ziwen, upon returning from abroad, will fully understand the situation and change course, adhering to the original intention of

aiding Chinese merchants, and seeking low-interest loan solutions. However, it is expected that Japanese merchants will not be willing to purchase all the cotton, and the small amount of American cotton purchased for competitive purposes will not harm Chinese merchants. As for the Chinese-owned cotton mills, they do not oppose the government's cotton loan initiative, but are most concerned about

the use of the funds. People buy cloth to make clothes, cotton mills spin yarn to weave cloth, and American firms like Anderson, Clayton & Co. pre-order American cotton for spinning. In essence, people create a multilayered leak to make clothes. Now, the government purchases American cotton, requiring repayment of principal and interest over five years. If managed well, it can reduce the leakage and generate profits. The cotton price is 200 million yuan, with a term of five years. If the government uses this fund for construction projects, only needing to allocate 1% to cotton planting, the effect would be immediate and the benefit significant. Production could increase dramatically, and cotton prices would stabilize. Wouldn't this be a great policy? Otherwise, the cotton funds'

whereabouts would be unknown, and after five years, the people would have to bear the repayment, essentially making people pay the price of two sets of clothes for one set. This is why there is so much concern. Currently, the government has not indicated anything to the cotton mills, and it is uncertain whether the cotton mills have the ability to purchase cotton at a high price and spin low-priced yarn. Everything depends on Minister Song Ziwen's return and the relief measures he proposes before deciding on the extent of adoption.

Growing Unrest over Fixed-Quota Tax on Tobacco and Alcohol 143

Earth-yellow wine and Shaoxing wine industries have ceased production and transportation.

Soy sauce and rice wine industry decided to suspend operations after stocks are sold out.

Since the Ministry of Finance's Tax Affairs Department abolished the public monopoly on tobacco and alcohol and implemented a fixed-quota tax on July 1, despite consistent efforts by the tobacco and alcohol industries and chambers of commerce to seek relief, the earth-yellow wine industry has ceased production and transportation. The Shaoxing wine industry has decided to suspend operations after its inventory is sold out. The unrest is spreading. Details are as follows:

Shaoxing Wine Transportation Halted. The Shaoxing Wine Industry Association stated that the public monopoly on tobacco and alcohol has been in place for twenty years. Now, the Tax Affairs Department has issued new regulations, abolished the public monopoly, and increased tax rates, causing members' Shaoxing wine shipments from Shaoxing, Zhejiang, to various places to be detained, resulting in irreparable losses. Forcing them to affix stamps and pay taxes is a disguised form of likin (internal transit tax). The association's repeated appeals were ineffective, making it impossible to operate. The association has decided to unanimously halt the transportation of Shaoxing wine from Zhejiang to various places and has reported the suspension to the United Association for assistance.

Earth-Yellow Wine Production Stopped. The Earth-Yellow Wine Industry Association stated that the Tax Affairs Department's new fixed-quota tax regulations require immediate stamping of all produced wine, increasing tax rates and severely impacting business. After repeated appeals were ineffective, they were forced to suspend production starting August 1 and reported the suspension to the United Association for assistance. As a result, all earth-yellow wine workshops in Pudong have closed, causing panic among winemaking workers. The Winemaking Workers' Union submitted a petition to the City Party Headquarters and the Social Affairs Bureau, requesting relief to prevent workers from losing their jobs.

Soy Sauce and Rice Wine Industry to Suspend Operations. The Soy Sauce and Rice Wine Industry Association issued a declaration stating that since the Tax Affairs Department abolished the public monopoly and implemented a fixed-quota tax, members of the soy sauce and rice wine industry have been uneasy. They were willing to reluctantly accept a slight increase in tax rates, but complicated procedures and frequent penalties have made merchants fearful. The fixed-quota tax is too idealistic and impractical. The authorities were aware that it could not be fully implemented and stipulated that implementing details would be separately formulated according to each province's situation as a remedy, proving that the fixed-quota tax regulations are not immutable. Furthermore, the Tax Affairs Department repeatedly stated that it would accommodate commercial interests and discuss the matter at length. Those handling tax collection should uphold the intention of higher ups, consider the circumstances, and benefit both tax revenue and commercial interests. It should not be handled with trickery to deceive the authorities. Unfortunately, the wrong people were used, and they acted unilaterally, inciting a few industry miscreants to disregard the public opinion of legitimate trade associations, leading to the unfortunate suspension of transportation and brewing by the Shaoxing Wine and Earth-Yellow Wine industries. The Earth-Yellow Wine industry's resolution is a painful one for the Soy Sauce and Rice Wine industry. After deliberation, the executive and supervisory committee decided to convene a members' meeting on August 4 to discuss the matter. After deliberation, it was resolved that, in addition to fully accepting the first point regarding storage and transportation issues, they would contact various wine industry groups to jointly fight for relief. If no effect is achieved and the source of wine is cut off, they would uniformly suspend operations and await a solution. It is believed that the intention of changing the tax regulations was to eliminate corruption and rectify tax revenue, and that they would not want one or two individuals to make a big mistake and disregard the livelihoods of millions of people. In the event that the unrest escalates and unfortunate incidents occur, affecting local security, they are willing to bear the responsibility and request that justice be upheld and that the people's lives be protected. Therefore, they hereby urgently inform all soy sauce and rice wine businesses in the city to immediately stop transporting all wine stored in various workshops. After selling off existing inventory, uniformly suspend operations to show their determination. This is the declaration.

Further Appeals. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency met with Zhang Dalian, executive director of the Soy Sauce and Rice Wine Industry Association, who stated that since the Tax Affairs Department implemented the new fixed-quota tax regulations, the Earth-Yellow Wine and Shaoxing Wine industries have been unable to bear the harsh taxes and have successively suspended production and transportation. The Soy Sauce and Rice Wine industry will be forced to suspend operations due to the interruption of supply. This is truly a last resort. In addition to requesting assistance from various sectors, they have decided to wait for Minister of Finance Song Ziwen to return to the country and then submit a petition to fight for relief, continuing until the goal of abolishing the fixed-quota tax is achieved to alleviate the difficulties of merchants and the people.

The Chamber of Commerce Federation Telegraphs the National Chamber of Commerce Federation Regarding the Harsh and Cumbersome New Regulations on Special Tobacco and Alcohol Taxes. Yesterday, it telegraphed the Ministry of Finance again, requesting the abolition of the regulations and the issuance of revised regulations. The original text is as follows: To the esteemed Ministry of Finance in Nanjing: It has come to our attention that the new regulations on special tobacco and alcohol taxes are harsh, cumbersome, and impractical. The association previously received telegrams from the Jiujiang City Chamber of Commerce in Jiangxi Province and the Siming County Tobacco and Alcohol Industry Association in Fujian Province requesting that the regulations be abolished and revised. The association telegraphed your ministry on July [blank] and [blank] of this year, requesting action. Today, we also received telegrams from the Wuxue City Chamber of Commerce in Hubei Province, the Shanghai Earth-Yellow Wine Industry Association, the Soy Sauce [blank] Industry Association, the Soy Sauce and Rice Wine Establishment Association, the Shaoxing Wine Industry Association, and the Liang [blank] Wine Trade Association.

In addition, representatives from various public organizations in Susong County, Anhui Province, came to the association and stated that the sales of local wine have been severely impacted by the dumping of American products and the interruption of the route to the Northeast. Farmers and workers who depend on it for their livelihoods are on the verge of collapse, and local wine is also affected by foreign wine, with business gradually declining. Now, the public monopoly has been changed to a special tax, and the tax rate has increased, even exceeding the selling price. Furthermore, they are ordered to pay the new tax on inventory that has already paid the old tax, making it impossible for merchants and the people to maintain their businesses. As a last resort, they have no choice but to suspend transportation and brewing to show their determination. They request that the goods that have already paid the old tax be exempted from the supplementary tax and that new regulations be revised. Upon receiving this, we found that the abolition of the old tax on the public monopoly of tobacco and alcohol and the issuance of new special tobacco and alcohol tax regulations were originally intended to unify the tax laws. Although the tax laws have been changed, the tax rates cannot be increased. Now, under the guise of changing tax laws, the reality is to increase tax rates. At this time when farmers, workers, and merchants are struggling with the precarious business of local wine, imposing heavier taxes that exceed the selling price is tantamount to cutting off their livelihoods. Moreover, the business of local wine is gradually declining due to the import of foreign wine, and what it relies on to survive is actually that its price is cheaper than foreign wine. Now that the tax rate has been increased and coupled with harsh and severe penalties, it seems that the government's intention to maintain commercial development has been lost. As for the goods that have already paid the old tax, ordering them to pay the new tax again violates the legal principle of not prosecuting past offenses. Moreover, before the new tax was issued, the old tax had already been paid, which means that the obligation to pay taxes has already been fulfilled. Due to sluggish sales, the goods have been accumulated to this day, and the warehouse rent and interest have already caused unbearable losses. If the new tax is levied again, it is a case of adding insult to injury. Because the association has witnessed the difficulties, we dare not hide them from the higher authorities. We hereby telegraph your ministry again to review the matter and request that the new regulations be abolished and revised, ensuring that both national plans and the people's livelihoods are considered. This is our earnest plea. Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Chamber of Commerce Federation, kowtows.

Declaration of Forced Workers of the Da Wan Bao 144

Dear compatriots, it is common in today's society for capitalists to oppress workers. Unexpectedly, the authorities of the Da Wan Bao are now using their insidious "discarding the bow after the birds are gone" tactics, wielding the power of capitalists, and seeking to put us to death. To fight for survival and justice, in addition to continuing to adhere to our consistent principles and fighting with the capital side based on reason, we can only make the general course public to society, and respectfully ask colleagues and the social sector to sympathize with us and provide strong assistance, so that weak workers and their families will not starve to death, and justice can be maintained. At that time, the authorities of the Da Wan Bao brought people to Tianjin, repeatedly stating how excellent the treatment of the Da Wan Bao was and how generous the wages were. Their sweet words and promises exhausted their ability to lure us with bait. Thinking of the desire and hope of the pitiful workers with weak knowledge and heavy burdens to "earn more money to support their families," the clever capitalists, the Da Wan Bao authorities, saw through the weaknesses of the poor and weak workers and took the opportunity to attack. Of course, who among us did not have hopes? And batches of us were caught on his hook and entered his snare, and successively left the work of the Tianjin Yong Bao and other newspapers, and came to Shanghai and joined the Da Wan Bao one after another. When we first arrived in Shanghai, it was when the Da Wan Bao was still under preparation, and it was also during the fierce "January 28th" Sino-Japanese war. We worked hard for the Da Wan Bao under the dangerous situation of rattling airplanes, booming artillery fire, and lives at risk in the morning and evening, never questioning. We ask ourselves if we have ever let down the Da Wan Bao authorities, but the world is full of people with unpredictable intentions, sinister means, and despicable actions, which, however, are shown by the well-dressed, so-called leaders of the press. The Da Wan Bao authorities, on the one hand, used the extremely tense period of the "January 28th" incident when people were eager for news, and on the other hand, tempted the workers to work hard, so that the newspaper took the lead in all Shanghai evening newspapers in less than a year. The Da Wan Bao's ability to develop so quickly and its plans to be so smooth are due to the efforts of the operators and, without being modest, mostly due to us workers! Suddenly, the Da Wan Bao authorities, for some unknown reason, suddenly declared to the factory on August 7 through manager Chen Yaozhu: "This newspaper is now in order to save expenses. From now on, the newspaper will be entrusted to the Shishi Xinbao for production. You workers who came to Shanghai from Tianjin at that time, there were three batches in succession. Now, according to the order of the authorities, the first batch will be temporarily retained here to be assigned to other affairs, and all the second and third batches of workers will be returned to Tianjin." What? What is this? Alas, the foundation of the Da Wan Bao is consolidated, the capitalist's pockets are full, the capitalists have no worries from now on, and they are deeply afraid that the workers will have any demands. Therefore, they implemented their preemptive poisonous plan and ignored the life and death of the workers. Who does not know that the Da Wan Bao and the Shishi Xinbao are two-in-one? Therefore, the newspaper authorities' insidious "discarding the bow after the birds are gone" tactics can be said to be a familiar trick, but this time it is applied to us who have traveled across mountains and rivers and have no way to retreat from our hometowns, which is even more ruthless and vicious. And their divisive tactics of temporarily retaining the first batch and dismissing the second and third batches are obvious. Now we can only fight with them at the cost of our lives. Our demands are not extravagant, we have no faults, but we only ask them to restore the original state and continue to work as usual. There is no need for the newspaper to save expenses. As for the coping strategies, if negotiations fail, we will inevitably find other appropriate ways to cope. However, workers have limited knowledge and weak strength, and during this struggle period, we hope that all colleagues and insightful people in society will take the warning of "the rabbit dies, the fox is sad" and give us practical and strong assistance, so that those who are dying will not die. The virtue of rebirth will be forever appreciated with endless gratitude. This is our declaration. The Committee of Forced Dismissal Workers of the Da Wan Bao weeps.

The Tax Affairs Department Explains the Fixed-Quota Tax Regulations for Local Wine 145

The Government's Rationale

Since the Ministry of Finance's Tax Affairs Department in this city changed to collecting fixed-quota taxes on local wine, the Shanghai Liang (Distilled) Wine Trade Association has repeatedly protested. The department yesterday issued an instruction to the Jiangsu Stamp Tax and Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau, explaining in detail the seven points raised. The original instruction is recorded below: For the matter of instruction: It is reported that Huang Yuming, chairman of the Shanghai Liang Wine Trade Association, stated in his presentation that the changes in the public monopoly have harsh and cumbersome clauses that hinder commerce, requesting amendments or continued handling according to the old regulations, and attaching a detailed list of opinions. Based on this, it is found that the change to fixed-quota tax for local wine is for the purpose of consolidating the original fees and taxes of various provinces for unified collection. The method focuses on uniformity and simplifies procedures. All regulations on the fixed-quota tax for local wine have been submitted by the Ministry of Finance to the Executive Yuan and then to the National Government for the record, and have been announced and ordered to be followed. The provincial businesses, not understanding the regulations, have repeatedly submitted requests to postpone or amend them, and clear instructions have been issued and sent to the bureau for compliance. Now, after reading the chairman's presentation, there are still many misunderstandings. The first point regarding the procedures for large [blank] repackaging and affixing repackaging inspection certificates has already been separately regulated. Repackaging already taxed and affixed with certificates for retail sales in the local area does not require affixing another tax payment certificate, and this has also been clarified in a separate order, so there should be no difficulty, and there is no such thing as "one product, multiple taxes." The second point regarding taxation by weight has always been handled this way. The old regulations did not stipulate a starting point of 50 catties. If it were as stated in the presentation, then small [blank] and bottled wine produced locally and containing less than 50 catties could all be exempted, which is impossible. The third point regarding the scattered retail sale of small quantities, with irregular containers, and without sealing, the number of inspections is tight. If each piece were counted and certified, the procedures would be too trivial. Therefore, the new regulations change to checking and determining the number monthly, originally to accommodate business conditions. If this causes suspicion that when bulk sales are sluggish, they cannot be transported elsewhere, then all products can be packed into containers, sealed and certified, and a separate counter can be set up to open the seal for retail. Winemaking shops must not sell in bulk retail, so that they can be shipped out at any time. The fourth point regarding the time limit for transfer has been approved in the joint petition of the Shanghai-Nanjing-Suzhou Tobacco and Alcohol Industry Association, and the bureau will handle it at its discretion and submit it for approval. The fifth point regarding the starting point of 50 [blank] catties has no such provision in the regulations, as stated above. The sixth point regarding Article 23 of the new regulations, that those who temporarily stop brewing must seal the vats and stoves, and Article 24, that those who cease operations must destroy the ponds and stoves, the former refers to temporary suspension, and the latter refers to complete closure. The boundaries are very clear, and most provinces handled it this way under the old regulations. The chairman of the association, not having read the entire text of the new regulations, mistakenly believes that temporarily stopping brewing also requires destroying the ponds and stoves, no wonder it is difficult to implement. The seventh point regarding the fixed-quota tax rate is determined by consolidating the original taxes and fees of various provinces and collecting them uniformly. The old regulations for the public monopoly calculated the rate based on price, and market prices fluctuated constantly, easily leading to abuses. Therefore, it was changed to a fixed-quota tax based on quantity, specifically to facilitate merchants and is not comparable to increasing taxes. The Zhejiang vat tax is another item collected during the public monopoly era. In addition, there were also tobacco and alcohol donations, brewing household licenses, inspection fees, and other items collected at the same time, which have been in place for a long time. Since the new regulations were implemented, they have all been canceled, and only the fixed-quota tax is collected, simplifying the process, and the superiority of the new system lies in this. The presentation cites the weaknesses of the old tax as an excuse to hinder the new regulations, not only reversing the cause and effect, but also being ignorant of the facts. As for the new regulations, the product is collected at the place of production, and the import is collected at the place of entry, all collected at one point, and no longer taxed within the province, simplifying the process, which merchants should be happy to follow. The presentation states that the audit of wine shipped to Shanghai was stricter at the point of entry than at the point of exit, so how can the various local wines be prevented from infiltrating sales? The Shanghai local wine tax system has a long history of accumulated malpractices and has almost become a breeding ground for abuses. The special printed certificates are especially used as amulets to evade regulations. Since all locally produced and imported wines must be taxed and certified, unscrupulous merchants have lost their reliance and are resisting in every possible way, especially fighting for the special printed certificates. After repeated severe rebuttals, they have gradually complied. If, as stated in the presentation, we continue to follow the previous habits and handle them flexibly, we will not achieve the benefits of centralization and will only open the door to omissions. What benefit would there be? In short, national taxation values simplicity and fairness. The old regulations were confusing and cumbersome, which cannot be denied. The business community in various provinces has repeatedly requested amendments, so the new regulations were revised, hoping to benefit both the national treasury and business conditions. If there are difficulties in the procedures, we have broadly adopted public opinions and made changes to be as appropriate as possible. This department has been considerate of all businesses and is truly meticulous. Merchants who are not familiar with the regulations may have misunderstandings, which is understandable. The chairman, being in a leadership position in the association, should be well aware of the tax situation, yet he is still pointing out everything in detail, and his wording is especially inappropriate. It is inappropriate to request amendments or continue to handle things according to the old regulations. Regarding the aforementioned situation, order that each point be refuted and instruct the bureau to severely reprimand and instruct all businesses to comply with the new regulations and not to wait and see under any pretext. This is the order.

Commander of the American Asiatic Fleet

Admiral Hepburn to Arrive in Shanghai to Assume New Post 146

The Da Mei Evening News reports that the new Commander of the American Asiatic Fleet, Rear Admiral Hepburn, will arrive in Shanghai to assume his new post. He will arrive next Monday on the President Van Buren or next Tuesday on the President Jackson. The outgoing commander, Rear Admiral Taussig, will immediately return to the country after handing over the command, taking leave until about October and then retiring due to age. As the headquarters of the Asiatic Fleet is far from the home country and the political situation in the Far East is unstable, the position of commander is known as one of the most complex and responsible positions in the U.S. Navy. Therefore, his power is also uniquely large, exceeding that of other fleet commanders. Rear Admiral Hepburn is highly respected and previously served as the Director of Naval Operations in the Navy Department, his importance being second only to the Chief of Naval Operations. Due to the importance of the Far East, he was specially selected as commander. He arrived in Japan several weeks ago with his wife on the President Coolidge, where they met with Japanese officials and American expatriates. It is uncertain whether Mrs. Hepburn will accompany him to Shanghai or continue her tour of Japan. The flagship Houston is scheduled to arrive in Shanghai from North China on Saturday morning, preparing for Rear Admiral Hepburn to board and take office within the next week.

Liuhegou Coal Mining Company

Issues 4 Million Yuan in Bonds 147

Has Been Filed with the Ministries of Finance and Industry

Currently in Negotiations with Banking Sector

For the purpose of developing its business, the Liuhegou Coal Mining Company in this city has specially submitted a request to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry, in accordance with the Company Law, to issue 4 million yuan in company bonds in Shanghai. It is currently in negotiations with the banking sector in this city for underwriting, and it is expected that it will be launched on the market soon. The face value is divided into three types: 500 yuan, 1,000 yuan, and 10,000 yuan. The annual interest rate is set at 8%, and the principal and interest will be repaid in ten years. According to Gong Fengxiang, business director of the company, speaking to a reporter from the Xin Xin News Agency yesterday, the company's issuance of company bonds this time is entirely for its own business and is currently in progress. The company's mine is located in Henan, and it specializes in the production of bituminous coal. The entire workforce is approximately 5,000 people, and the average daily coal production is more than 2,000 tons. Unfortunately, since 1927, transportation on the Pinghan Railway has been hampered due to military influence, and the produced coal has been unable to be sold externally, causing the company's economy to be severely impacted. During these years, the authorities have made great efforts to maintain the livelihoods of the miners. Although transportation on the Pinghan Railway was restored in 1932, freight rates increased, so the accumulated losses were very large. The purpose of this bond issuance is to consolidate small amounts into larger amounts in order to settle some old debts.

Social Affairs Bureau and Public Safety Bureau

Relief Efforts for Victims of Pudong Fire 148

Temporary Porridge Distribution by Police Stations

Seeking Public Places for Temporary Shelter

Instructing Local Leaders to Notify Disaster-Stricken Households to Register

Local Gentry to Request Construction of Low-Income Housing

Zhang Yigen, a native of Yancheng living at 76 Nancaonitang, Pudong, accidentally started a major fire while cooking the other day, causing an unprecedented disaster. Details have been reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that Yang Zhongquan, director of the Third District, First Precinct of the City Public Safety Bureau, considering that thousands of victims have been displaced after the fire, which is very pitiful, has instructed the police to purchase 12 shi (ancient Chinese unit of dry volume, equivalent to about 100 liters) of rice to provide porridge to all victims temporarily, maintaining the status quo. Regarding the aftermath, at 8:30 yesterday morning, Zhang Binghui, Section Chief of the Fourth Section of the Social Affairs Bureau, dispatched staff member Sui Zhao, along with Yin Guanzhi, Director of the Relief Division, and Zhang Boqin, staff member of the Household Registration Division, dispatched by Hong Qi, Section Chief of the Second Section of the City Public Safety Bureau, to investigate. Yang Zhongquan, director of the First Precinct of the Third District of Pudong, led them to inspect the area for a week and then returned to Shanghai at 12:00. Upon arriving at the Social Affairs Bureau, they consulted with Chen Lengseng, Director of the Relief Division, and others to discuss relief measures. It was decided that: 1) Director Yang should instruct local leaders to notify all disaster-stricken households to register their names and numbers of people first, and to temporarily maintain the situation while consulting with local gentry and dispatching police to find public places nearby, such as temples, for accommodation as much as possible; 2) If it is deemed necessary to build temporary shelters, then report to the Public Safety Bureau and the Social Affairs Bureau for approval. As for temporary relief measures, the Social Affairs Bureau will consult with Wang Yiting, chairman of the United Association of Charity Organizations, to find ways to provide relief, so as to prevent the victims from being displaced. It is reported that the local gentry in Pudong will submit a request to the city government to build low-income housing. Also reported, the fire in the Caotang area between Yangjiadu and Laobaidu in Pudong burned down more than 500 houses the day before yesterday. Because most of the residents there are poor people from Jiangbei, after the disaster, more than 2,000 people were displaced and were in a terrible state. The authorities have built shelters as temporary accommodation for the refugees, and the Dongtai Association of Fellow Townsmen in Shanghai is planning for the aftermath. Starting yesterday, they will first provide porridge and rice, and it is also heard that the meeting plans to convene various public organizations in Pudong to discuss the restoration of houses and various safety issues.

Foot-Pedaled Vehicle Robbed in Broad Daylight on Zhongshan Bridge 150

Police and Thugs Engage in Fierce Gunfight

One-Eyed Robber Surrenders

A portion of the bridge surface of Zhongshan Bridge, No. 4 Zhongshan Road, Zhabei, is currently damaged. Therefore, the Municipal Works Bureau is currently trying to repair it as quickly as possible. All vehicles passing over the bridge must proceed slowly. Yesterday at around 1:00 PM, Dai Yougen, who grows flowers in Miaotou (i.e., Pengpu Town), was riding his own bicycle from east to west to Miaotou Garden for business. When the bicycle reached the end of the bridge, Dai got off and pushed the bicycle across the bridge to prevent damage to the bridge construction. Unexpectedly, after Dai crossed the bridge and had only walked a few steps, a person suddenly stepped forward to block his path, claiming that he was carrying private goods, and searched him thoroughly. Finding nothing, the thug, not wanting to leave empty-handed, pulled out a handgun and told Dai that he was sorry and wanted to borrow his bicycle, and warned him not to make any noise, otherwise he would use the handgun, etc. After speaking, he got on the bicycle and sped off towards the east. At that time, there were several plainclothes security team members nearby who inquired about the situation and blew their whistles wildly. Wang Shifu, the squad leader of the 4th District Public Security Bureau's detective team, along with detectives Fang Chaofu and others, were on patrol. Police officer Tian Xiancheng from the Tanziwan branch station also pursued one after another. The thug, realizing that things were not going well, panicked and fell off the bicycle, hitting his left eye corner on the bricks and stones, causing profuse bleeding. Seeing that the police and security team were close behind, he drew his handgun and fired wildly. The police officers also took cover by the roadside and returned fire several times. After a fierce battle lasting several minutes, the thug was apprehended and a White Langlin handgun, No. 61386, was seized. There were still three bullets in the gun. The detectives, considering that the location was under the jurisdiction of the Tanziwan branch station, handed him over to Officer Tian to take to the station and escort him to the 4th District for interrogation. According to the thug, his name was Yao Afu, 42 years old, from Haimen, and he lived in a small inn on Sixth Malu in the concession. The rest of his words were cunning. The interrogating officer, seeing that Yao's eye corner was injured, ordered him to be sent to Pushan Hospital for bandaging first. Unexpectedly, upon closer inspection, the thug's right eye was already blind. He was wearing a white short shirt, and his entire body was covered in blood. He is currently being held in the 4th District for interrogation.

Carpenter in Longhua Hejing Town Sets Fire Out of Revenge 151

More Than Twenty Thatched Houses Destroyed

Public Security Bureau Currently Investigating

The home of Cao Ximing, a local farmer at No. 3 Zhu Jia Bridge, Cao Jia Garden, Hejing Town, Longhua, suddenly caught fire at around 8:00 AM yesterday. In an instant, flames burst through the roof, spreading to neighboring houses. Fortunately, the nearby patrol police received the news, reported it to the station chief, who instructed the fire brigade to rush pump trucks to the scene to extinguish the fire. French Concession Authorities Actively Eradicating "Poison Pills" 152

Catching Those Who Catch Themselves, Selling Those Who Sell

Dispatching More Detectives to Strictly Enforce Day and Night

Recently, the sales of "red pills" in this port have been so widespread that, according to those familiar with the matter, the daily sales volume actually surpasses that of opium. However, upon examining its origins, the French Concession is the place where it all began. Among them, the most reputable and widely sold is the "No. 11" brand of red pills. These poison pills were originally created at No. 11 Yu Kang Lane, Route Pichon, in the French Concession. As sales increased, it was named after the location. Recently, the police authorities of the French Concession have been extremely strict in investigating and prohibiting red pills. Anyone caught manufacturing, selling, or consuming red pills is sent to court for severe punishment. The police have now discovered that these retail red pill sellers have been using Zilaihuo Street, Ruifu Lane, as their base. Like cunning rabbits, they change their hiding place several times a day, sometimes in the lane, sometimes in the middle of the road, as well as in cigarette shops and snack stalls. There have been daily arrests. Therefore, the patrol chief has dispatched more Chinese and Vietnamese patrol officers to patrol the area around Zilaihuo Street and Ruifu Lane day and night, and has also sent undercover agents to patrol the alleys at night to eliminate the toxic atmosphere.

Patrol Officer Opens Fire and Wounds Detective 153

Detective Was a Thief

Four Shots Fired, Injuries Very Serious

Hu Jili, detective No. 329 of the Huishan Police Station in Tilanqiao, suddenly received a tip at around 7:00 PM last night, claiming that thieves were hiding in a certain house in Jun'an Lane, Yuezhou Road, planning to commit robbery. After receiving the report, Hu reported to the patrol chief and dispatched the entire armed detective team to arrest them. Upon entering the house, they indeed saw eight or nine thieves gathered and talking. Upon seeing the detectives, they scattered like birds and beasts, trying to escape. The detectives then rushed forward and captured five of them on the spot, and also confiscated firearms and other items in the house. The other four thieves took the opportunity to escape through the back door. One of them, wearing a blue cloth shirt and trousers, ran barefoot along Yuezhou Road from north to south towards Zhoujiazui Road. Upon seeing this, Detective Hu immediately led the detectives in pursuit, blowing his whistle wildly to warn the patrol officers. At the same time, the detectives with guns fired at the thief. However, the thief was agile and dodged the bullets. Seeing that the pursuit was very close and whistles were blaring, he turned east from Zhoujiazui Road and fled towards Zhoushan Road. Detective Hu, disregarding his own safety, held his handgun and ran ahead, leading the pursuit. At this time, two Chinese patrol officers, No. 2144 and 1952, were on duty at the intersection of Zhoushan Road. Seeing a person in short clothes and a person in long clothes running towards them, with detectives chasing behind, whistles blowing frequently, and gunshots intermittent, they knew something was wrong and quickly prepared for action. When the two people ran up to them, they saw that Detective Hu was still tightly holding his handgun and running forward, about three or four feet away from the person in short clothes, but he never fired his gun. In Detective Hu's mind, he hoped to capture the thief alive. Unexpectedly, Chinese patrol officer No. 2144, seeing Detective Hu wearing long clothes and holding a handgun, running in front, mistakenly thought he was an accomplice of the thief. He pulled out his service pistol and fired four shots at the two people in front, two of which hit Detective Hu. As a result, Hu fell to the ground, bleeding profusely, and the thief still escaped. At this time, the detectives behind had already tracked them down and saw Hu lying on the ground, covered in blood. Believing that he had been attacked by the thief, they quickly unbuttoned his shirt, intending to first remove Hu's bulletproof vest. It was then that Chinese patrol officer No. 2144 realized that he had mistakenly wounded Hu. He quickly reported to the police station and sent a car to rush Hu to the patrol police hospital for treatment. After examination by the hospital, it was discovered that he had two injuries, one in the neck, which was very serious, and one in the right arm. Afterwards, four shell casings from the Chinese patrol officer's gun were recovered at the scene of the incident and are now being held in the police station. They will be interrogated after Detective Hu's injuries have healed. The five thieves who were captured are also being temporarily held in the police station while they wait to apprehend the other accomplices and handle the case together.

Shen Shunfa's Strange Case of Looking for a Wife and Losing Her 154

A Er and A San Conspire to Abduct a Married Woman

False Benevolence, Alas, the Heart of a Woman

Shen Shunfa, 25 years old, from Wuxi, used to make a living by farming in his hometown. With the encouragement of his parents, he married a woman surnamed Wang from Wuxing through a matchmaker. After she joined the family, the relationship between the couple was still harmonious. However, because Shen's family was not very wealthy, it was often difficult to solve the problem of firewood and rice. Therefore, not long after their marriage, Wang came to Shanghai alone in 1930 and worked as a maid for a certain family through an introduction, lasting for more than two years. Recently, she was laid off and temporarily resided in Wu Baoji's employment agency at No. 1147 Triangular Street, South City, and asked for an introduction to an employer. A man from Haimen named A Er, over 30 years old and not yet married, who worked as a cart driver in the Shangnanchuan Salt Guild Hall near the employment agency, often went to the agency to chat during his free time. He saw that Wang was young and beautiful, so he often made suggestive remarks and frequently tried to seduce her. Before long, the two of them became entangled in a scandalous affair. Unexpectedly, good things are often difficult to come by. Recently, Shen heard about the matter and rushed to Shanghai yesterday to Wu Baoji's employment agency to order his wife to return home. Wang firmly refused, and secretly discussed with A Er to temporarily appease her husband, and when Shen took her to the pier to board the ship, she would take the opportunity to escape to his house, and gave her two yuan for travel expenses. Wang was overjoyed with the plan, and returned to the shop, falsely claiming to Shen that she was now willing to return home. Shen then accompanied her to Lao Laji Bridge. A Er suddenly remembered that he had now secretly instructed Wang to escape to his house, but he did not yet know the address of his house. He quickly wrote a note, writing down the address of his house, and asked a female acquaintance from Wuxing, Yan Yangshi, to catch up and hand the note to Wang. He also ordered his younger brother, A San, to secretly follow behind Shen and others, waiting for an opportunity to lead Wang away. When Shen and others arrived at Lao Laji Bridge, they boarded the inland small steamer and waited quietly for departure. However, Shen suddenly felt that the weather was hot, and fearing that he would be thirsty on the way, he asked Wang to wait on the steamer, and he went ashore again to buy a watermelon nearby, and brought it back to the steamer, preparing to cut it in the middle of the journey to quench his thirst. Unexpectedly, when he returned to the boat, Wang had already disappeared. He searched everywhere, but there was no trace of her. It turned out that when her husband went ashore to buy a melon, Wang had been led away by A San. Shen recalled that Yan Yangshi had given Wang a note, which was very suspicious, so he returned to Yan Yangshi's place to question her. She told the truth, and Shen realized that Wang must have been abducted by A Er. He rushed to the Salt Guild Hall to inquire about A Er's whereabouts, but the hall replied that A Er had now returned to his hometown. Shen was anxious, and took Yan Yangshi to the First Section of the First Precinct to request a thorough investigation. The Section Chief conducted a preliminary hearing and ordered a written report to be submitted to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Post Office to Offer Telegraphic Remittance Endorsements 156

Shanghai Post Office News: The bureau now, in order to meet public needs, starting from September 1st of this year, in addition to the ordinary fees charged by the post office, will charge a telegraph fee of one dime per word (two dimes per word for English). The remitter of a telegraphic money order will be allowed to add a short endorsement to the telegram to the payee within the money order telegram. However, the post office will not be responsible for any errors in this endorsement due to translation or retransmission.
