Talking Points

Reporting Oneself 243

"A bald daughter, her mother always says she's good!" This is an unbreakable iron law. Human beings tend to have this common disease: being critical of others and forgiving of themselves, seeing the bad things in others but not reflecting on their own mistakes.

Of the maids in the mouths of wives, nine out of ten are bad. For example, if the young mistress loses her Western doll or the husband's silk scarf is clearly abandoned at the dance floor, the disaster star is sure to be blamed on the maid. It's as if they saw it, saying that she stole it to sell it for melon. They won't think about their own people, let alone investigate.

Even in the children's brawl dramas that often take place in the alleys, the adults on both sides always come forward and make a big scene. Some do scold their own children a few times, or even beat their own children to vent their anger, "It's your own fault. I told you not to mix with them!" This tone is clearly further blaming the other party.

Capitalists and factory directors only know that workers are complete bad eggs. Seeing that in this era of "intensified unemployment terror," it is not enough to have work. They want to improve their treatment. When petitions have no results, they encourage labor unrest, strikes, and sabotage. If the factory is closed, what way out do you have? They don't think about the factory's difficulties at all. Therefore, absolutely, capitalists will not realize that their exploitation is wrong.

They indulge in their own waywardness, visiting prostitutes and playing with women. But as soon as they see their wife or concubine chatting with the kitchen administrator next door, they immediately put on a serious face: "You filthy ×× be more careful, don't blame me for being ruthless!" At this time, of course, they won't remember their own lascivious behavior.

When a few friends get together, they talk at length, and everyone points out the faults of others, and they are eloquent, and they are never seen to confess their own bad habits.

The general intellectuals play this tactic even more, as if the more knowledge they grow, the cleaner they protect themselves.

Old scholars can point out the shortcomings of young people in a coherent way and say that vernacular writing is as ordinary as speaking. However, they cannot find that they have become a wart in the "evolution" process. The articles they write are not only not in line with the facts, but also grammatically incorrect, making people dizzy at first sight.

There are even more writers, as the saying goes: "One's own wife is always uglier than others', but one's own articles are always better than others'." They specialize in settling accounts with others, and they are afraid of not being able to praise themselves to the sky, to be immortal. Just open a magazine and look, there are always several such writers and articles.

The general young compatriots are even more loyal models of blaming others and forgiving themselves. For example, when it comes to life, they have already squeezed into the middle class and are constantly rushing and falling into dance halls, movie theaters, ice rooms, cafes, and food stores. Yet they keep shouting for themselves, blaming society and others, without thinking at all that those who are scraping for a living on the streets are also people and are also surviving.

Such behavior is indeed a flaw in human beings, so I want to shout loudly: "Report yourself!"

I Love Summer 244

— Bin Fu

丨An Unexpected Love Affair丨

Now it is summer again.

Summer, after a separation of three seasons, has returned, and I feel joy. Among the four seasons, I love summer the most. Summer is grand, summer is solemn, summer is natural, and summer is full of poetic sentiment. It is when summer arrives that the lonely world is adorned with liveliness; it is when summer arrives that the cold society is imbued with vitality. Summer exposes the beauty of nature, and summer dissipates the coldness of the human world. The bright and beautiful spring is the season for young masters and misses to talk about love, which is not for us. The clear and refreshing autumn day is the perfect time for famous literati and elegant scholars to discuss romance and the moon, which is also not for us. As for the cold winter, we, who have had our fill of the coldness of the human world, are indeed very ordinary. It is only summer that can give us a universally and appropriately enjoyable experience of the characteristics of the season, so I love summer.

Now that summer has arrived, I am happy.

How lovely are the softly buzzing mosquitoes that appear in summer! They are constantly by people's sides, morning and night, singing. Is the young master Ji's lover's pearly throat so melodious? Is the Prince Wang's "darling's" affection so lingering? Every day when I return to my room from work, they immediately fly to my side in groups, intimately. When I take off my sweaty shirt to bathe, they rush to help me suck up the sweat; when I collapse wearily on the canvas cot to rest, they come to sing by my ear, sometimes burrowing into my arms, sometimes crawling on my arms and neck. The innocent mosquitoes sometimes tickle me, and I often jump up from the tickling. Only then do they giggle and buzz away. I was born with an irritable temper. When I get tired of playing with them, I often hit them. The cunning ones among them, of course, fly away buzzing as if they are pretending to be cute. The weak ones are often slapped to death by me. Alas, these good singers and dancers cannot withstand the swat of my giant palm, and they all turn into beautiful blood-like red stains. These red stains decorate my white summer cloth mosquito net. The scattered remnants of red are truly a beautiful and delicate painting!

I love that mosquito girl who is both a painter and a poet. I love summer even more. I wish that mosquito girl would always be by my side. I wish summer would last forever in the human world.

Let those dignitaries, wealthy gentry, and rich tycoons stay forever on Mogan Mountain, which "has no summer." Let us enjoy the greatness, solemnity, and beauty of this summer as long and fully as possible.

"Vienna" Pilgrimage 245

— Jian Xun

Cars sped down Jing'an Temple Road like arrows, the neat rows forming a gray line, silently and windingly advancing toward their magnet—"Vienna"—in the rustling rhythm of wheels on asphalt.

On the ruins of the Dahua Hotel, a soul-stirring kingdom has been built here. The brilliance of the "Yearly Red Lights" interweaves into a rainbow-like net, trapping "Vienna" and also trapping the longing of passersby outside "Vienna."

The aroma of beer and Luzon cigars fills the entire space. The gray-black bamboo fence marked "Vienna Common Garden Dance Hall" surrounds countless gentlemen and women in circles.

Here: there are fields and fields of the wealthy, that irregular area of golf; filled with tempting colors and patterns; red, green, square, slanted.

In the dance hall, pairs of young men and women dance embracing, smoothly gliding in fox trots on the glossy floor. The huge brass loudspeaker shines with golden light, illuminating everyone who is intoxicated in the light-green haze.

Jazz music plays intermittently, and the light melody of "Fan O Ling" is as beautiful as moonlight.

Here: one cannot hear the wailing of the 30 million compatriots in the Northeast under the iron heel of the imperial army, nor can one hear the sobbing of the hundreds of millions of hungry people scattered in our vast and rich land. Here, one only hears gold and flesh playing a magnificent symphony.

People all over the world, listen: Who says China is extremely backward in material things, and Chinese people are all coolies? Look! Isn't this place crowded with countless noble men and women enjoying all modern material comforts?

Film Special

A Scene of Degeneracy 246

— Xian

Afternoon, a summer as long as a year.

Miss Three woke up from her afternoon nap. The electric fan on the desk covered her cloud-like beautiful hair over her face. Seeming languid and weak, she pushed her hair to her ears, stretched out her hands, straightened her snake-like slender waist, and with a pair of eyes turning under her long, slender eyebrows, she drowsily recalled a sweet dream. Suddenly, as if remembering something, she called her maid, A Cui.

A Cui did not expect that Miss Three would wake up so early. She was flirting and joking in the garage. The young lady's call was so low. Looking at the bedroom door, and still not seeing A Cui coming in, she jumped up from the leather sofa, blew on herself in front of the electric fan for a while, and slowly strolled to the dressing mirror. The face powder on her face had been condensed into a film by the sweat. "A Cui," she shouted loudly.

A Cui was called from the garage by Cai Ma, who said that the young lady was angry upstairs. Thinking that the young lady had discovered her secret, she went upstairs with a heavy heart. Miss Three was really impatient. "Where did you die? Quickly bring two bottles of soda!"

A Cui took the soda and went back upstairs. Miss Three was lying on the sofa again, holding a cigarette and thinking about something in a daze. A Cui poured a full glass of soda and placed it on the small tea table without paying attention. A Cui had no choice but to stand there blankly. For a while, the room was as lonely as a late autumn morning, with two hearts pondering two different things.

The cigarette burned Miss Three's pointed fingers. Turning her head, she saw A Cui standing there blankly.

"What are you standing there for!"

"Miss, the soda."

"I know, go run the bathwater!"

"Miss is taking a bath?"

"If not taking a bath, what else would I be doing!" Miss Three was always loud and bossy today.

She raised the glass and took a sip of the soda. "Icy," she muttered as she went to the bathroom.

She took off her silk pajamas, and a charming young girl's body was exposed in the mirror. Miss Three jumped into the bathtub as if she was being peeped at. She again thought of that sweet dream, "A Cui," she called.

A Cui turned the door knob. She did not come in because the door was not locked. She smiled and said through the door, her voice not as loud and bossy as before:

"Go downstairs and listen for the phone, A Cui, don't let Madam hear!"

A Cui smiled at her own guilty conscience. How would the young lady know her secret? Thinking about the unexpected extra money, her steps were much lighter when she went downstairs.

When A Cui came upstairs again, Miss Three had finished putting on makeup, with her right leg crossed over her left, sitting peacefully on the sofa, but her heart was not so calm, which could be seen from her rolling eyes.

A Cui leaned over to Miss Three's ear and whispered for a while. Miss Three only smiled and nodded, stood up, looked at her body in front and behind in the mirror, and walked away as if doing a fox trot.

Seeming disappointed, A Cui rushed to the door and said to the young lady, "Do you need a car?"

Miss Three gave her a meaningful look, took a banknote from her handbag, and handed it to her, "A Cui, if Madam wakes up, say that Miss Six asked me to play mahjong again, and I'm going to see a movie tonight, so there's no need to send a car to pick me up!" Miss Three shouted deliberately loudly.

"Understood, Miss," A Cui's tone also became louder.

Shop Employee Correspondence

A Female Worker's Production Tribulation 247

Editor:

I am an ordinary shop employee. I have already benefited quite a bit from your column's teachings. I feel very puzzled by not seeing any correspondence in the Shop Employee Correspondence column for several days. Your column is probably not stopping like the Readers' Consultant, is it? I have another matter to trouble you with. Please take the time to answer it.

I am married, my parents are both alive, and I have four younger brothers who are all unmarried. The youngest is only fourteen years old and still studying. The rest are employed, but their income is very meager. My father is fifty years old and still in good spirits. He runs a small shop in the countryside, barely making a living. In the past, when the market in Shanghai was prosperous, my income was still good, and I was responsible for a considerable portion of the household expenses, which I could still maintain. Since the war in Shanghai, the economy has been sluggish, and rural areas have gone bankrupt one after another. Prices are falling day by day. Our store has suffered a lot. Especially since our store specializes in wholesale to other places, business has plummeted. Fortunately, our boss has managed things properly, so the overall situation has not been affected. However, we employees have always relied on the year-end bonus from the store's profits. Now that the hope of a bonus is gone, and we have no savings, we cannot maintain the original situation. Therefore, last year, I ordered my wife to come to Shanghai to work in a factory. Although the income is meager, it is still a small supplement. Unexpectedly, my wife is about to give birth, and there will inevitably be another expense at that time. Moreover, she will not be able to go to work in the factory after giving birth. Therefore, after thinking about it again and again, there is no safe solution. I have always admired your enthusiasm for teaching, so I dare to bother you with this letter. I hope you will not refuse. I humbly ask you to write back. With best wishes, Pan Min, sincerely (August 3rd)

×××××

Editor's Note: Since this column was launched last year, it has been praised by people from all walks of life. I dare not spare any effort to help my dear shop employees in any way possible. A few days ago, due to important matters in the editor's family, it was difficult to explain hastily, and no one was asked to fill in, so it was interrupted for more than a week. I am very sorry to have troubled readers with inquiries. In the future, it will continue as before.

In these difficult times, "fewer people producing and more people eating" is definitely not going to work. The fact that your wife is working in a factory is very much in line with the times. Don't be misled by the terrible word "face" and worry about it. In our opinion, your family can really boast, "There is no one eating idle rice." Except for the youngest brother who is not yet an adult, everyone can support themselves. Even your parents, who are over fifty years old, are still struggling to make a living. On your part, you can already be said to be "doing your best," but the result is still inevitable panic. This is the evil result of the social economy and uneven distribution. This is also the result of someone exploiting in the middle.

Your wife will soon give birth. Temporary expenses and subsequent impacts put you under economic pressure everywhere. When a group of neither old nor new people hear about it, they will inevitably complain to you, saying that you are overestimating your abilities and why didn't you adopt the method of "birth control." In the editor's opinion, their words are absolutely wrong. Look, any kind of animal in the world can live and reproduce leisurely. Is it possible that humans, who are the spirit of all things, can only live a hard life after years of hard work, and even the God-given desire to procreate must be forcibly suppressed? Moreover, broadly speaking, the people of China are poor. Then, can we advocate national "birth control" to cut ourselves off from humanity? We believe that our way out is to unite the exploited and attack the exploiters, reclaiming our due rights. For example, regarding the issue of female workers' childbirth, we can demand that the factory pay wages before and after childbirth. We sell our entire lives to capitalists. Anything we need for life cannot be dismissed as out of line.

The above method is a fundamental solution, and it cannot be achieved in a short time. Mr. Pan may inevitably dismiss it as "high-sounding." A passive method is to seek help from charitable organizations (such as civilian maternity hospitals) when labor begins. After childbirth, you may as well send your child to someone else to raise. We don't necessarily have to raise our own children ourselves; it is enough to be satisfied with the "desire to procreate" if my child lives in this world.

Fiction

Under the Traffic Lights (50) 249

— Xi Lin

(27) This is a Sign of China's Revival

When Shi Qiao was standing on the street corner, holding the letter and stunned with excitement, he suddenly heard the sound of firecrackers from far to near, gradually as if the sound of firecrackers ignited. Like a fuse, the whole city immediately responded. At first, he wanted to inquire about the reason for the firecrackers with a kind of war-time terrifying psychology, but before he could ask, he saw a large group of people in front, holding up the national flag, rushing up like a tide, and the sound roared:

'Long live the Republic of China, long live the great Chinese victory!'

'Then the shouts from all around surrounded them!'

'Shirakawa is dead, General ××× has arrived in Shanghai!'

'Recover Zhenru, capture Zhabei!'

Everywhere was a mixture of cheers and firecrackers, resounding through the heavens and the earth. Children, women, and old men all ran to the road. Everyone came out happily. Everyone forgot to close their doors, but no one would go in to steal. At this time, as long as they were Chinese compatriots, everyone was especially kind and more upright. Women stood by the roadside and waved their handkerchiefs to the crowds shouting slogans. Children scurried between the legs of adults, and if they were knocked down, they would get up and walk away without cursing at anyone. The old man stroked his beard, smiling and touching the head of his grandson. He was sixty or seventy years old and had never seen such a happy and encouraging grand occasion. Shi Qiao only seemed to have split his mouth with laughter, but he still couldn't close it. He asked about the news along the way, how Ishikawa died, and when General ××× arrived. Everyone was willing to answer him loudly, partly because the shouting on the road was noisy and could not be heard unless they spoke loudly. Some told him that Ishikawa was stabbed to death by our soldiers with random guns, some said he was killed by artillery fire, and some said he was assassinated by a Chinese female warrior when the enemy held a celebration. This female warrior was a graduate student from the Imperial University of Japan who spoke Japanese. She disguised herself as a Japanese dancer, mixed into the celebration, and threw a bomb at Ishikawa, killing him. It was also said that General ××× led the strategic army in a battle that defeated the enemy in an unknown way. Zhenru has been recovered, and in the battle of Liuhe, thousands of enemy troops were killed, three airplanes and six cannons were seized, and countless spoils of war were obtained. When Shi Qiao walked to Avenue Joffre, the excitement there was even more spectacular. The shops on both sides, whether they were Chinese goods stores, cigarette and paper stores, fruit stores, silk and satin stores, pharmacies, foreign goods stores, department stores: : : : All the electric lights were turned on as much as possible, dazzlingly shining, and all were hung with national flags. Looking at a row, they formed a red and blue oblique line, neatly and strangely beautiful. The shop assistants stood at the door, competing to set off firecrackers, crackling and popping, thousands of sounds and harmonies, red flames blooming everywhere. Even more, many people threw firecrackers down from upstairs or hung them up with long bamboo poles to set them off. The crowds walking below scattered for a while and then gathered again with laughter. The smell of gunpowder permeated. The trams in the middle of the road were crowded with people, and the tram windows were full of heads, waving and shouting. In the blink of an eye, another tram of people came by, shaking and shouting. They even sang the national anthem, and the people on the roadside responded. The cars coming and going were like schools of fish, forming groups and speeding by. All the cars of Shanghai's car dealerships must have been rented out. Every car had a national flag, and some even had naked men standing on the roof, making heroic gestures and shouting to kill ×××. The muscles of their whole bodies revealed a powerful outline. That kind of healthy and beautiful posture obliquely symbolized the powerful Chinese nation. Inside the carriages, they were beating gongs and drums with all their might. Many children took the opportunity to climb on the sides of the cars and cling to them, or climbed on the rear wheels behind the cars. Some fell down and climbed onto the second car. Teams of people walking were also beating gongs and drums. The national flag was in the front and back. Look! The anger of a nation that has been oppressed for so long, the melancholy of a century that has been lurking for so long, has erupted in a roaring, roaring voice from the depths of the earth!

Shenbao Local Supplement Film Special

History of German Cultural Films (Part 2) 250

— Hou Feng

The "Film Bureau" has the following two methods of rewarding generally excellent films: First, it is stipulated that films must be deemed suitable for educational purposes by the "Film Bureau" before they can be screened in schools. Second, films with standard value may be screened in ordinary cinemas, and their entertainment tax will be reduced or exempted. The German film viewing tax is generally stipulated at 15% of the ticket price. However, films that have passed the inspection of the Film Bureau can receive preferential treatment and obtain reductions or exemptions.

The personnel of the "Review Board," namely the "Film Bureau," are mostly government officials, and its content includes representatives from the Ministry of Culture, the Ministry of Agriculture, and the Ministry of Health. Its main financial resources come partly from the collection of film review fees, and partly from the income of issuing permits. At the same time, the association also has the establishment of an inquiry office to answer the questions of general manufacturers, distributors, and powerful people in the private sector regarding art films, educational films, cultural films, and other issues. Although the association cannot produce or distribute films itself, it has established methods for guiding filmmakers in order to correct the evils of bias, and it also examines scripts in advance before films are produced. At the same time, it strives to make teachers and school administrators understand the value of cultural films so that they can lead students to appreciate excellent films. Therefore, it also published a teaching syllabus and implemented a film technology training institute for teachers, and the classification of educational films. The so-called German Film Association is responsible for managing the rental or sale of films and projectors to member schools. It has many branches within Germany. At the same time, it maintains a close relationship with the Central Film Bureau. The total number of schools in Germany is about 80,000, and the number of schools that actually implement film education is more than 20,000. As mentioned above, the German cultural film policy can be said to be not far from the road to success, but in reality, it is not optimistic. Waludenru·Jiedenru said this in his "Dead German Educational Films": "The German economic depression is too profound. Although the German teachers' joining the school film alliance has an economic foundation as its background, it cannot be denied that they are driven by a desire for fame. Some school teachers are still cursing their encouragement of their families to help the school's games, harming their children: : : :. At the same time, we can observe from the theoretical standpoint of the foundation of educational films that, in order to achieve the purpose of continuous activities, various methods and stages should be studied first. However, the current Germany does not even have the smallest amount of 'gold,' so the school can only use the donations from the 'Parents' Association' as the cost of screening films. On the police side, however, there is a great power to list prohibitive regulations. They check what kind of permits there are, what the entrances and exits are, what the indoor lighting is like, and how the projector should be positioned. Therefore, teachers cannot but avoid it for their own comfort. : : :"

The entire history of German cultural films and educational films is a process full of hardships and difficulties. It is a chronicle full of blood and filth. However, since Hitler seized power this year in March, rumors have spread that the National Socialist Party is already manufacturing political propaganda films. And German cultural films have also encountered a major historical shift. (End)

Film Commentary

Review of "The Mysterious Beauty" 251

— Ling He

The Girl in 419

Jameson is a star who finds it difficult to earn money, which is probably not a problem. Therefore, producers never miss such a good opportunity; as long as it is at all possible, Jameson always has to star in various new films. Regarding his work, we probably won't forget "Good Luck" which he starred in with Sally Shou Luan. In this film, we can see that he is indeed very good at comedy performances, and has a unique flavor. As for films like "Considerate," they are ultimately unremarkable and lack any characteristics, although they are not offensive.

In these works, we can clearly find his artistic characteristics; almost every one of his works is the same: the characters he plays are often optimistic and frivolous young people. Of course, the content of individual films varies somewhat, but the characters he portrays are almost cast from the same mold. As mentioned earlier, the director of "Good Luck" cleverly grasped his characteristics, allowing him to give full play to his abilities under the conditions of a funny sailor. As for the authors of the latter, such as "Considerate," although they wrote the script for him, he could not succeed in more serious dramas.

"The Mysterious Beauty" belongs to the latter category. He is just singing his old tune, and it can't be said to be a success; at best, it is passable. So here we can see that using stars to attract audiences is indeed the ultimate method for film entrepreneurs, but the achievements of stars do not necessarily fully satisfy people.

As for the entire play, the director's ability here is only to present a monotonous story with a slight twist. However, the confusion of scenes and the fragmentation of editing make each scene tell the plot, rather than acting well. This disjointed combination of short shots certainly cannot grab the audience's attention and make the play a success.

However, the main failure is still the tastelessness of the story. Writing scripts for stars is already a very tasteless thing, let alone turning tricks within the same content. The story tells of a doctor who, after falling in love with a nurse, accidentally falls in love with a female patient from a bandit gang. As usual, talented scholars and beautiful women must become a couple. Thus, this doctor from the police hospital abuses his power for personal gain to acquit the girl living in room 419. He even shows favoritism to the bandit because of this. In the end, a method of retribution is used, causing the bandit to die at the hands of another doctor, which reveals the ridiculousness of anarchy. Perhaps some people will say that this is their own exposure. However, this is also a naive view, because advanced artists will never engage in such seemingly right but actually wrong nonsense.

Audience Opinions

Talking About The Radiance of Motherhood 252

— Ni Qiu

Consciously, this is a work that depicts people in general who are devoted to art for money. It satirizes women's vanity and the so-called artists' desire for money, which can be described as incisive.

The actors in this film are all very hardworking. Chen Yanyan plays a girl who has been baptized by vanity, and her attitude is very natural. Li Zhuozhuo's style has become very good, but unfortunately she lacks opportunities in the first half of the film, and her performance is inevitably repetitive. She is very good at showing the suffering of a mother in her heart regarding Xiaomei's behavior. When she hears Jiahu describe the situation of hard labor, the inner compassion she displays is completely realized. Duo Yan's style in this film is very similar to Novarro's performance in Ben Hur. The revolutionary enthusiasm fills his entire body, and the paternal love hidden behind when he meets Xiaomei is also very sincere.

The other supporting actors are also suitable for their roles. The interweaving of Liu Jiqun, Han Langen, and Yin Cenxi's actions, such as clapping, taking off hats, and throwing flower baskets, are all very novel.

The director's efforts are even more evident in this film. Several shots, such as Mr. Zou holding back tears as he bids farewell to Xiaomei and leaves, taking out a handkerchief at the exit, and the scene of Liu, Han, and Yin reading the newspaper, and when the mother boards the ship to go abroad to see her daughter, only the father is seeing her off at the dock, are all very capable of leaving a deep impression on the audience.

The subtitles in this film are indeed a great enhancement to the film. For example, when Ji Mei asks Mr. Zou whether he has made a fortune in Nanyang and returned, Mr. Zou's answer reveals the global economic downturn, as well as the status and oppression of overseas Chinese today, which is indeed very meaningful.

Other aspects, such as the sound of the last song being well recorded, and the photography being better than "New Year's Eve," show that Huang Shaofen's skills have indeed made significant progress.

Impressions After Watching "The Radiance of Motherhood" 253

— Luo Ping

In such a morbid society, under economic pressure, it is a very common fact for a woman who has lost her husband to remarry someone else with her children.

Of course, the reason for this remarriage is not necessarily for vanity and enjoyment, but for her own survival and for the survival of her children. If Huiying remarried for enjoyment and vanity, then she could have abandoned her child. From this, we can see the unique love of motherhood.

Huiying's heart is permanently tied to Xiaomei. However, her daughter, influenced by her father's education, and seduced by material things and vanity, insists on marrying a wealthy man as his wife, and cannot comprehend the mother's heartfelt love at all. But when she is ill in Nanyang, her mother specifically finds a way to get money and goes to Nanyang alone to see her. This can also show the great love unique to motherhood.

In real society, the "love" between men and women is considered sacred and inviolable on the lips of some people, and their life in the words of some people. However, in reality, women are only treated as toys by playboys. Huang Shulin's abandonment of Xiaomei is an inevitable phenomenon under this social system. Therefore, after Xiaomei exposes the mask of the wealthy and gives birth to a son, she will truly realize who is sacred, great, and affectionate in the love between men and women and the nature of motherhood. Therefore, "The Radiance of Motherhood" is not only not feudal preaching, but also clearly explains everything in this society.

Talking About "The Radiance of Motherhood" 254

— Xiang

Regarding the actors in "The Radiance of Motherhood," Chen Yanyan, who plays Xiaomei, shows surprising progress in her performance. Every move and gesture is suitable for the character in the play, and she has achieved considerable success. Li Zhuozhuo, who plays Xiaomei's mother, has changed her style, and although some parts are too rigid, it is still good. Jin Yan's performance as Jiahu is also very profound, but Lu Shi's performance as Ji Mei is too contrived. He Feiguang, Li Junpan, and Ying, etc., are also good. On the whole, the actors can still fit the personality and identity of the characters in the play.

In terms of plot, although the record Xiaomei sings is well-known, I don't think even old men and maids would follow the music and dance. This is too excessive and unrealistic a depiction!

The maids in Huang Shulin's residence in Nanyang seem to not be dressed like maids in Shanghai. I think this is also a very minor flaw.

In terms of photography, the light is not soft enough in some places, but there are also several shots that are very satisfactory.

Other aspects, such as the humorous interludes of Liu Jiqun, Han Langen, and Yin Xiucen, the performance of Xiaomei's daughter Lian Jiang, from a lively and lovely young child, the innocent and unrestrained nature of the children in the nursery, and the beautiful little bird singing "The Radiance of Motherhood" at the end, can all add to the brilliance of this film.

In short, this film reveals the greatness of maternal love and can truly be called a rare domestic film.

Film Novel Morning Glory (3) 255

— Ma Teng

He thought, why reject people from a thousand miles away? It wouldn't hurt to lend a helping hand. So he agreed to have an in-depth conversation with Yi Fan. Later, Hedges became very interested in recommending her to Eiston or Seymour Bossamore.

At this moment, a blonde girl suddenly walked in. She was very arrogant, and the many people sitting outside the office were not in her eyes. She came in and went straight inside. Yi Fan, while asking "Who is this?", assessed her and felt that this woman was arrogant and frivolous. The woman walked past Hedges, and Hedges stood up respectfully and bowed to her, but she just nodded as if she didn't care. Eiston's assistant, Mr. Seymour, came out himself to greet the woman and took her inside. Yi Fan asked Hedges again, as if impatiently, who that woman was and whether she could act. Hedges told her, "That's Rita Vernon. Of course, she can act." But Hedges' tone was cold. He also said, "She has a talent for performance, but she's also too lucky. Her future is very bright, but it's a pity that she's too arrogant and indulgent."

In the inner room of the office, the habitually arrogant Rita Vernon was issuing orders to Eiston; and the writer Sheridan, knowing that he had deep disagreements with Rita Vernon, was hiding in the bathroom next to the office. He didn't want Rita Vernon to join his play, but for Eiston's sake, he couldn't firmly oppose it. And Eiston didn't admire Rita Vernon that much either, but felt that she still had some appeal. The play "Blue Sky," which is now being rehearsed, has to let Rita Vernon play the lead role. But Sheridan always hoped to find a suitable lead role in his recent translation of Mona's "The Golden Bough," so that he could become famous in one fell swoop. He could let Rita Vernon play the lead role in "Blue Sky," but when "The Golden Bough" was rehearsed in the future, he absolutely could not give in again.

But this was just Sheridan's wishful thinking. He hadn't heard Rita Vernon giving Eiston the following ultimatum yet. The condition she put forward to Eiston was: she would now accept the lead role in "Blue Sky," but after "Blue Sky" ended, she should choose which play to rehearse next and which role to play herself. Eiston had no choice but to agree to her. He thought that "Blue Sky" would take a lot of time to rehearse. When it came time to rehearse "The Golden Bough" later, he would think of other ways. He sent the protagonist away and sighed deeply.

Rita Vernon went out, and Eiston hurriedly asked Sheridan to come out; but as soon as Sheridan's foot stepped out of the bathroom door, Rita came back in, putting Sheridan in a dilemma and making him very embarrassed. (To be continued)
